8.1.2
Standard ELISA procedure
The reagents and procedure for conducting ELISA originates from a combination of the
product datasheet from R&D Systems [72], the manufacturer of the ELISA kits used, and
previous experimental optimisation of the assay conducted in the CBIO Group at DTU
Nanotech. The applied procedure described below is the general procedure used for all
ELISAs in this project.
Coating plate with capture Ab: Capture Ab was prepared to working concentration in
PBS. A 96-well Nunc MaxiSorp microplate was coated with 50 µl diluted capture Ab
solution per well and the plate was tapped to ensure proper spread of the solution in each
well. The plate was sealed with an adhesive strip and incubated overnight at 4  in the
fridge.
Blocking and adding sample to plate: The following day, the plate was washed three times.
The washing was done inverting the plate and removing any liquid already in the well,
adding 100 µl Washing Buﬀer to each well, gently tapping the plate to ensure proper
spread of added wash buﬀer, inverting the plate and blotting it against a clean paper
towel. The plate was blocked by adding 150 µl Reagent Diluent to occupy any binding
108
==PAGE:129==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
sites of the well not bound by capture Ab to limit unspeciﬁc binding. The plate was sealed
and incubated for minimum 2 hours at room temperature. After incubation, the plate was
washed three times as per above instruction. 50 µl incubation sample, standard, controls
etc. were added to each respective well, potentially diluted before sample addition to
the plate. For standard IL-6 samples, typically prepared in wells A1-H2, 50 µl Reagent
Diluent was added to well B1-H2 and 100 µl 2000 pg/ml IL-6 standard was added to wells
A1-A2. A two-fold dilution was constructed by repeated transfer of 50 µl sample down
rows A-G. The 50 µl taken from wells G1-G2 was discarding, leaving 50 µl in all standard
wells and H1-H2 as blank samples. The plate was tapped to ensure spread, sealed and
incubated overnight at 4  in the fridge.
Assay development: The plate was washed three times. Detection Ab was prepared by
diluting to working concentration and 50 µl detection Ab solution was then added to each
well. The plate was tapped, sealed, covered with foil to protect from light and incubated
for 2 hours at room temperature. Wash was repeated and 50 µl diluted Streptavidin-
HRP solution was added to each well. The plate was tapped, sealed and incubated for 20
minutes at room temperature covered with foil. Wash was repeated and 50 µl Substrate
Solution was added to each well in fume hood and incubated and covered with foil for
approximately 5-15 minutes. Incubation time depended on speed of colour change to
turquoise and 50 µl Stop Solution was added to each well to stop colour development,
turning the sample liquid from turquoise to yellow. The plate was shaken lightly to ensure
mixing and was placed in the Victor multilabel plate reader. Absorbance of samples were
measured at 450 nm and 570 nm to correct for optical imperfections in the plate. IL-6
concentrations were calculated as described above using Equations 3.1 and 3.2.
8.1.3
Incubation procedure
The general procedure applied for all incubations related to ELISAs is described below
with signiﬁcant adjustments detailed separately.
Start-up of incubation: Each incubation series was prepared according to a setup similar
to the outlined in D.1. To reference sample wells, 50 µl buﬀer was added with 100 µl
buﬀer in Pefabloc-only samples. To IL-6+ wells, 50 µl rh IL-6 was added. Subsequently,
50 µl Cat G was ﬁrst added to all Cat G+ reference samples followed by addition in
IL-6+/Cat G+. Immediately following reagents addition, the plates were gently tapped to
ensure proper mixing in the wells and were placed at the assigned incubation conditions.
Stopping reaction: After 15, 30, and 60 minutes incubations were stopped, done by ad-
dition of 50 µl Pefabloc to the appropriate wells, see Appendix D.1. To the remaining
wells, 50 µl buﬀer was added.
Transfer to ELISA: 50 µl sample from each well was transferred to the corresponding well
on the ELISA plate constituting the ’added samples’ in the ELISA procedure.

==PAGE:130==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
8.2
SDS-PAGE
8.2.1
Materials and reagents
The following reagents and materials were needed for performing sample incubations as
well as the analysing SDS-PAGE: XCell SureLock® Mini-gel electrophoresis system cell,
ThermoFisher (Cat. # EI001); NuPAGETM 10 % Bis-Tris 1mm 10-well gel, ThermoFisher
(Cat. # NP301PK2); NuPAGETM 12 % Bis-Tris 1mm 10-well gel, ThermoFisher (Cat.
# NP341PK2); Sample Buﬀer Laemmli 2x Concentrate, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # S3401);
PageRuler protein ladder 10-180 kDa, ThermoFisher (Cat. # 26617); Spectra protein lad-
der 1.7-40 kDa, ThermoFisher (Cat. # 26628); NuPAGE® MES running buﬀer, Thermo
Fisher (Cat. # NP0002); SimplyBlueTM Safestain, ThermoFisher (Cat. # LC6060); rh
IL-6/CF, R&D Systems (Cat. # DY206-IL/CF); Human leukocyte Cat G, Sigma Aldrich
(Cat. # C4428); Human neutrophil Cat G, Athens Research (Cat. # 16-14-030107); Hu-
man leukocyte NE, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # E8140); Pefabloc, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. #
76307); 20 mM Tris / 50 mM NaCl TBS buﬀer pH 7.4; 100 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4.
8.2.2
Procedure
The following general procedure applies to all conducted experiments involving SDS-
PAGE. Some experiments involved sample incubations prior to SDS-PAGE analysis and
the procedure for this is described as a Incubations separate step. Hence, for SDS-PAGE
samples that did not undergo incubation, this step does not apply.
Preparation of gel: The gel pack was opened and the gel was rinsed with dH2O and placed
in the electrophoresis cell. The gel tape was removed prior to insertion. MES running
buﬀer was poured into the centre compartment, covering the gel wells. The remaining
buﬀer was poured into the outer compartment. 500 ml running buﬀer was used in total.
The comb was removed slowly from the gel and the wells were washed by pipetting run-
ning buﬀer up and down into the wells.
Incubations: For non-incubated samples, this step did not apply. In 200 µl Eppendorf
tubes, a total of 20 µl sample was incubated. First, buﬀer was added after which IL-6 was
added at appropriate concentrations in the respective tubes. Finally, Cat G was added
and immediately following Cat G addition, the tubes were placed in a Thermoshaker at
37  with shaking at 300 rpm.
Preparation of samples/stopping reaction: The following steps applied to all run exper-
iments, but also constituted the stopping of the reaction for incubated samples except
for SDS-PAGE experiment 2, see Table 3.3, where reaction was stopped by the addition
of 5 µl 0.1 mM Pefabloc solution. After 15, 30, 60 or 120 minutes the incubations were
stopped by addition of 5 µl SB, constituting a 1:4 ratio between SB and sample volume.
Samples were heated at 70  at 500 rpm for 10 minutes in a Thermoshaker.
Loading samples and running PAGE: 5 µl protein ladder and 25 µl sample were loaded
into the designated wells. The PAGE was initially run at 80V for 5 minutes to stack sam-
ples followed by 150V for 50-70 minutes. The PAGE was stopped once the sample dye
reached the bottom of the gel. The electrophoresis cell was opened and the gel cassette
was rinsed with dH2O.
Development of gel: The cassette was opened, the gel was removed from the cassette and
washed three times with dH2O in a plastic container. After wash, SimplyBlueTM SafeS-
110
==PAGE:131==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
tain was added to the plastic container and the gel was left staining for 1 hour, shaking
at 120 rpm at RT. The staining liquid was poured oﬀ, the gel was washed with dH2O
three times and was left in dH2O overnight (O/N) for destaining, shaking at 120 rpm at
RT. After destaining, the gel was imaged by use of a LI-COR Odyssey® FC gel imager
at 700 nm.
8.3
MALDI-TOF
8.3.1
Materials and reagents
For the experiments involving MALDI-TOF, the following materials and reagents were
used: rh IL-6, R& D Systems (Cat.
# DY206-IL/CF); Amicon Ultra-0.5mL 3 kDa
centrifugal ﬁlter, Merck Millipore (Cat. # UFC5003); ZipTip C18 pipette tips, Merck
Millipore (Cat. # Z720038); Sinapinic acid (3-(4-hydroxy-3,5-dimethoxyphenyl)prop-2-
enoic acid); Anhydrous ACN, 99.8 %; Triﬂuoroacetic acid (TFA), ≥99 %; Ammonium
bicarbonate; 0.5 g/L Trypsin-EDTA sterile solution, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # T3924).
8.3.2
Procedure
Measurement of samples on MALDI-TOF: All samples measured by MALDI-TOF under-
went the following procedure. Prepared protein sample for measurement by MALDI-TOF
was mixed with matrix solution at the appropriate dilution in a 0.5 ml eppendorf tube.
The tube was vortexed to ensure solution mix. 0.4 µl sample was spotted on the MALDI-
TOF 384-spot target plate. The spotted samples were left to dry before insertion into
MALDI-TOF machine. Using a method calibrated using standard protein samples in the
range of 2-20 kDa proteins, samples were shot with 2000 shots with frequency 500 at >90
% laserpower. The detection range was set at 2-35 kDa. The subsequently generated
sample intensity spectrum was analysed.
Desalting by buﬀer exchange: Before MALDI-TOF analysis, desalted samples by buﬀer
exchanging were subject to the following procedure. 1 µl sample was mixed in 0.5 ml
dH2O and centrifuged at 14,000 g for 20 min using at Amicon Ultra 0.5 ml 3kDa cut-oﬀ
centrifugation ﬁlter. The wash and centrifugation was repeated a total of three times.
The ﬁlter was inverted and sample spun out, yielding 25 µl sample. The sample was
subsequently analysed by above procedure.
Desalting by ZipTips: Samples desalted using Millipore ZipTips were treated per follow-
ing before analysis. The procedure was adapted from the suggested approach provided
by Millipore. 1 µl sample was mixed with 1 µl TFA to ensure sample pH < 4. Using the
speciﬁed Millipore ZipTip C18 pipette tips, the pipette plunger was depressed to a dead
stop. Using the maximum volume setting of 10 µl, wetting solution consisting of 100 %
ACN was aspirated into the tip and dispense to waste. Aspiration step was repeated.
Twice, equilibration solution of 0.1 % TFA in dH2O was aspirated into tip and dispensed
to waste. Peptides or proteins were bound to ZipTip pipette tip by fully depressing the
pipette plunger to a dead stop and aspirating and dispensing the sample 7-10 cycles for
maximum binding of complex mixtures. Twice, wash solution 0.1 % TFA in dH2O was
111
==PAGE:132==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
aspirated into tip and dispensed to waste. To a tube, 4 µl of elution solution was dis-
pensed using a standard pipette tip. The elution solution consisted of 20 mg/ml SA in
0.1 % TFA/50 % ACN. Eluant was carefully aspirated and dispensed through a ZipTip
pipette tip at least three time without introducing air into the sample. The eluted sample
was analysed by MALDI-TOF.
SDS-PAGE band procedure: Fragments originating from SDS-PAGE gels were subject to
the following treatment before analysis. The method was based on previously reported
procedures [91, 136, 137]. From SDS-PAGE gels with incubated samples, bands of pro-
teins were cut and removed from the gel by use of a scalpel. As little excess gel as possible
around the band was taken while still ensuring that the entire band was removed. Gel
slices were transferred to a 2 mL eppendorf tubes and incubated in 50 mM ammonium
bicarbonate at 60  for 30 min. Subsequently gel slices were incubated in 50 mM am-
monium bicarbonate with 50 % ACN at 60  for 30 min. Gel slices were dried in the
freeze-drier O/N. Gel were reconstituted in 20 µl 10 µg/ml Trypsin in 20 mM ammonium
bicarbonate. Gels were rehydrated for 1 hour at 4  and then incubated overnight at 37
. Peptides in the gels were extracted with 0.1 % TFA/50 % ACN at RT for 20 min and
freeze-dried O/N. Gels were resuspended in 10 µl 0.5 % TFA and underwent desalting by
ZipTips and analysis as above.
8.4
Enzyme kinetics studies
8.4.1
Materials and Reagents
The following reagents and materials were used for conducting of enzyme kinetics ex-
periments: Human neutrophil Cat G, Athens Research (Cat. # 16-14-030107); Human
leukocyte Cat G, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # C4428); Suc-AAPF-pNA colorimetric substrate,
Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # S7738); 4-nitroaniline, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # 185310); Nunc Mi-
croWell 96-well optical bottom (non-treated) microplates, ThermoFisher (Cat. # 265301);
100mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4; Anhydrous Dimethylsulfoxid (DMSO).
Prior to ﬁrst use, Cat G from Sigma Aldrich was reconstituted in 100 mM Tris buﬀer and
Cat G from Athens Research in dH2O. Suc-AAPF-pNA substrate was dissolved in dry
DMSO. 4-nitroaniline was dissolved in a 10:10:80 dH2O:DMSO:HEPES, resembling the
reaction solution of Cat G and Suc-AAPF-pNA.
8.4.2
Procedure
All kinetic study experiments were conducted according to the below. For the experiment
with NP-Cat G, NP-Cat G replaced Cat G in the procedure.
Reagent preparation: Suc-AAPF-pNA substrate was prepared to a ﬁnal substrate con-
centration, [S], of 25 µmol/ml (15.616 mg in 1 ml DMSO). Athens Research Cat G was
centrifuged brieﬂy prior to ﬁrst being opened and was reconstituted in dH2O to yield a
100 µg/ml solution.
Kinetic experiment: In a 96-well microplate reagents, buﬀers and substrate was added to
the respective wells according to the scheme in Table 3.5. Prior to addition of 10 µl Cat
112
==PAGE:133==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
G, absorbance at 410 nm of the samples were measured as time zero measurements. 10 µl
Cat G was added to respective samples, starting from the lowest [S] working and towards
the higher [S]. Immediately following Cat G addition, the microplate was inserted into
the Tecan Microplate Reader. The absorbance at 410 nm was measured for two hours,
continuously every 30 seconds. Based on the measured absorbance, [pNA] was determined
based on a standard concentration curve.
pNA standard concentration curve: With initial [pNA] = 2.5 µmol/ml, a double-determined
2-fold dilution curve of pNA in 10:10:80 dH2O:DMSO:HEPES was conducted. The ab-
sorbance at 410 nm of each sample was measured and based on the known concentration
a linear concentration curve was established.
8.5
Nanoprecipitation and characterisation
8.5.1
Materials and reagents
For precipitation and preparation of NPs, the following materials and reagent were used:
NH2−PLGA−NH2 polymer, PolySciTech (Cat. # AI21); PLGA−NH2 polymer, PolySci-
Tech (Cat. # AI16); PLGA−NH2 polymer, PolySciTech (Cat. # AI017); PLGA−COOH
polymer, PolySciTech (Cat. # AP081); Anhydrous ACN; Anhydrous DMF; Anhydrous
THF; 15ml 50 kDa cutoﬀAmicon Ultra centrifugal ﬁlter, Sigma Aldrich (Cat. # Z706345);
Millex-Hydrophilic Polyethersulfone (HP-PES) 13 mm sterile 0.45 µm syringe ﬁlter, Merck
Millipore (Cat. # SLHPX13NL); Millex-HP PES 33mm sterile 0.45 µm syringe ﬁlter,
Merck Millipore (Cat. # SLHP033RS); 100 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4; 50 mM HEPES
buﬀer pH 7.4; 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 8.5.
8.5.2
Procedure
Nanoprecipitations and characterisations by DLS and ζ of all NPs were conducted using
the following procedure. Any alterations to the protocol are described accordingly.
Polymer dissolution: All glassware and vials were air-blown using in-house air.
The
crystalline polymer was mixed in a glass vial with the respective organic solvent, either
ACN, DMF or THF at the appropriate polymer solution concentration. Typically, 1 ml
polymer solution was mixed. The solution was vortexed extensively and sonicated for ﬁve
minutes to ensure proper polymer dissolution.
Nanoprecipitation: 5-10 ml dH2O, depending on the study, was added to an glass vial
and stirred with a magnetic stirrer at 800 rpm. To the stirring aqueous solution, 500
µl polymer solution was added dropwise at a rate of 1 drop per second. The glass vial
was covered with punctured foil and let stir at RT for minimum 2 hours, allowing the
organic solvent to evaporate. The solution was ﬁltered through a 33mm 0.45 µm HP-PES
syringe ﬁlter into a 50 kDa Amicon Ultra centrifugal ﬁlter and dH2O was added to total
volume of 10 ml. The solution was centrifuged at 3,200-4000 g (rcf) for 20-30 min at 4 .
Filtrate was removed from bottom of Amicon ﬁlter and NPs remaining in ﬁlter cake was
washed with 10 ml dH2O and repeatedly centrifuged. Wash was repeated at least once.
NPs in ﬁlter cake were reconstituted by addition of 1 ml 100 mM HEPES pH 7.4 or pH
8.5. Vigorous pipetting and wash of ﬁlter was conducted to fully reconstitute NPs. The
1 ml NP solution was removed from Amicon ﬁlter and ﬁltered through a 13mm 0.45 µm
113
==PAGE:134==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
HP-PES syringe ﬁlter into an eppendorf tube.
DLS and ζ characterisation: A disposable cuvette was blown with in-house air and brieﬂy
washed with dH2O. To the cuvette, 1515 ml dH2O was added together with 85 µl NP
solution. Using the Brookhaven DLS/ZetaPALS Potential Analyser NP sizes, PDI and
count rate, given in kcps, were measured by DLS, n = 3. For ζ measurement, the electrode
was cleaned with 70 % EtOH and rinsed with dH2O before use. The electrode was inserted
into the cuvette and ζ was measured, n = 6.

8.6.2
Procedures
Crosslinker coupling and Cat G conjugation using PLGA−NH2-based NPs
The following procedure has been used for coupling of crosslinking agents to the NP sur-
face and further conjugation of Cat G. The procedure has been optimised signiﬁcantly
during the course of NP development. The optimised steps, amounts of reagents, time-
frames etc. are reported and discussed in Table 4.2, providing basis for discussion of
reaction optimisation success.
PLGA−NH2-based NP core linker conjugation: Following nanoprecipitation of NPs, if
PLGA−NH2 NPs had been stored in other buﬀers than 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 8.5,
NPs were buﬀer exchanged using a 50 kDa Amicon Ultra centrifugal ﬁlter by centrifuging
solution at 3200 g for 20 min at 4  and reconstituted in 1 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer
pH 8.5. NHS-PEG4-Mal- or SPDP-linker, see Table 4.2 for quantities, was dissolved in
114
==PAGE:135==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
minimal amount of anhydrous DMSO. The linker was freshly prepared due to instability
of NHS-ester. To 400 µl NP solution, the linker was added. To a total volume of 1 ml,
50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 8.5 was added. The reaction tube was wrapped in foil and
incubated at RT for 1-2 h under light shaking. Linked NPs were ﬁltered and washed
using 50 kDa Amicon either Ultra or Pro ﬁlters and 10 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4.
Centrifugation was done at 3200-4000 g for 30 if Amicon Ultra ﬁlters were used or 60
min if Amicon Pro ﬁlters were used. Wash was repeated at least once. Linked NPs were
reconstituted in 1 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4. DLS and ζ were measured on the
linked NPs as previously described. SPDP linking quantiﬁcation was performed on linked
NPs as per below protocol.
Cat G activation: Commercial Cat G was washed twice prior to use by centrifugation us-
ing Amicon Ultra-0.5mL 10 kDa centrifugation ﬁlter with 0.5 ml H2O and spin at 14,000
g in a ﬁxed angle rotor centrifuge. See Table 4.2 for Cat G quantity. Cat G was prepared
in minimal amount of TBS. Either a 20-fold excess of T-CEP in TBS, relative to Cat
G or 500 µl 0.5 mg/ml DTT in TBS solution was added to Cat G solution which was
incubated for 1 h at RT to cleave disulﬁde bonds of Cat G. Excess T-CEP or DTT was
removed by wash with 10 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4 and centrifugation in 10 kDa
Amicon Pro ﬁlter for 1-2 h at 4000 g. Wash was repeated at least once. Enzymes were
reconstituted in 1 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4.
NP-Cat G conjugation: 5-15 µl linked NPs, see Table 4.2, were mixed with activated Cat
G solution in 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4 to a maximum total volume of 1 ml. Solution
was incubated at 4  O/N, wrapped in foil. SPDP linking quantiﬁcation was conducted.
The Cat G-conjugated NPs were puriﬁed by removing excess Cat G by centrifugation
using 50 kDa Amicon either Ultra or Pro ﬁlters and washed ﬁrst with 5 ml 50 mM
HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4 at least twice followed by 5 ml 50 mM HEPES/1.5 M NaCl buﬀer
pH 7.4. Centrifugation was done at 3200-4000 g for 30 min if Amicon Ultra ﬁlters were
used or 60 min if Amicon Pro ﬁlters were used. DLS and ζ were measured on puriﬁed
NP-Cat G conjugates and Cat G-conjugation was quantiﬁed by Micro BCA on NP-Cat
G conjugates, washing ﬁltrates and linked NPs.
SPDP quantiﬁcation
For quantiﬁcation of SPDP-linking on NPs, 75 µl NP-SPDP solution was mixed with 5
µl 20 mM T-CEP or 25 µl 3 mM DTT solution in TBS. Additionally, 75 µl NP-SPDP
solution was mixed with an equal amount of TBS. Both samples were incubated at RT
wrapped in foil for 30 min. Absorbance at 343 nm was measured for both samples. For
quantiﬁcation of Cat G-conjugated to linked NPs, the absorbance at 343 nm was measured
for NP-SPDP-Cat G-incubated samples as well as NP-SPDP-only samples. The molar
ratio of either SPDP linking or Cat G conjugation to NPs was determined by Equation
(4.1).
Cat G conjugation using PLGA−COOH-based NPs
500 µl PLGA−COOH-based NPs was buﬀer exchanged into 0.1 M MES buﬀer pH 5.0.
The NPs were mixed with NHS and EDC in a total of 2 ml MES buﬀer, see Table 4.2 for
115
==PAGE:136==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
quantities. Samples were incubated at RT for 2 h with gentle shaking. Linked NPS were
puriﬁed by washing twice with 5 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 8.5 and centrifugation with
a 50 kDa Amicon Pro ﬁlter at 4000 g for 60 min at 4  and reconstituted in 1 ml 50 mM
HEPES buﬀer pH 8.5. DLS and ζ were measured on linked NPs. Cat G, see Table 4.2,
was mixed with 15 µl NPs in 500 µl 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 8.5 and incuated O/N at 4
. Cat G-conjugated NPs were washed twice ﬁrst with 5 ml 50 mM HEPES/1.5 M NaCl
buﬀer pH 7.4 followed by 5 ml 50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4 at least twice and centrifuged
with a 50 kDa Amicon Pro ﬁlter at 4000 g for 60 min at 4  and reconstituted in 1 ml
50 mM HEPES buﬀer pH 7.4. DLS and ζ were measured on particles as well as Micro
BCA was used for Cat G conjugation quantiﬁcation on NP-Cat G conjugates, ﬁltrates
and NHS-activated NPs.
Micro BCA
NP surface-conjugated Cat G quantiﬁcation was performed as per product guideline [120].
The procedure provided basis for enzyme quantiﬁcation in a linear working range of 2-40
µg/ml:
A series of standard BSA solutions ranging from 0-200 µg/ml was prepared. Into a 96-
well optical-bottom microplate, 150 µl standard solution or sample was pipetted into a
microplate well. 150 µl Working Reagent (WR) was added to each well. WR consists of
a 25:24:1 mix of Micro BCA reagent MA:MB:MC. Plate was shaken lightly, covered with
adhesive strip and incubated at 37  for 2 h. Plate was cooled to RT. Absorbance was
measured at 560 nm on a microplate reader. By use of the standard dilution series and
generated standard curve, protein concentration of each sample was determined [120].

8.7.2
Cell handling and Western Blot procedures
The ensuing protocol was utilised for handling and treating of raw macrophages as well
as conducting Western Blot.
Seeding of cells: Raw 264.7 Macrophages were seeded in 6-well plates at concentration of
5 · 105 cells/well in 10 % FBS 1% P/S DMEM media to a ﬁnal volume of 3 ml. Cells were
incubated at 37  and 5 % CO2 for 48 h until 70-80 % conﬂuency was achieved.
Treating cells: Media was removed from wells and cells were pre-treated according to the
setup shown in Section 5.2.2 with 3 ml 10 % FBS 1% P/S DMEM media containing 100
ng/ml LPS for 4 h at 37 , 5 % CO2. In non-LPS samples, 3 ml media was added. After
incubation, LPS-containing media was removed and 3 ml media with either 0, 1 or 5
µg/ml Cat G was prepared and added to the respective wells. Cells were then incubated
for 24 h at 37 , 5 % CO2.
Recovery: After incubation, plates were centrifuged at 300 g for 10 minutes to separate
supernatant from cells. Supernatants were removed, stored on ice before being vortexed.
Subsequently, both 100 µl undiluted and 10-fold diluted supernatant sample were applied
onto a prepared ELISA plate. ELISA was conducted as described in Section 8.1. Cells
were scraped using 2 ml pre-chilled PBS, transferred to an eppendorf tube and put on
ice.
Protein extraction: Eppendorf tubes were spun down for 10 min at RT at 12000 rpm.
The supernatant was removed from the cell pellets and 200 µl protein extraction solution
was added to the pellets. The protein extraction solution consisted of a 1:1:98 protease
inhibitor cocktail:phosphatase inhibitor cocktail:protein extraction reagent mix.
Western blotting preparation: Cells were kept on ice, vortexed for 2 min and left on ice for
5 min. Vortex step was repeated three times. Samples were centrifuged for 10 min at RT
at 12000 rpm. Samples were added to PCR-tubes, vortexed and centrifuged brieﬂy and
117
==PAGE:138==
CHAPTER 8. EXPERIMENTAL METHODS
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
subsequently 10 µl sample buﬀer consisting of 1:9 2-mercaptoethanol:4x Laemmli buﬀer
was added to each sample. Samples were heated at 95  for 7 min.
Preparation and running of gel: The gel cassette containing a NuPAGETM 4-12 % Bis-
Tris 1mm 15-well gel was removed from packaging, rinsed with dH2O and placed in PAGE
chamber. The inner chamber was ﬁlled with 1x Tris/Glycine/SDS (TGS) buﬀer with the
remaining TGS buﬀer poured in the outer chamber, to a total of 800 ml. To the far-left
well of the gel 5 µl protein ladder was added. PCR tubes were allowed to cool to RT and
20 µl sample was loaded into each respective well. The gel was stacked at 60 V for 15
min and subsequently run at 115 V for 1.5 h.
Transfer onto PVDF membrane: PVDF membranes were pretreated with 100 % MeOH
in a plastic container and shaken for 2 min, then washed with dH2O for 2 min and shaken.
Foam pads were soaked in 20% MeOH/Tris/Glycine (TG) buﬀer. A transfer sandwich
of foam pad:ﬁlter paper:gel:membrane:foam pad was stacked and placed in the transfer
cassette so that the membrane faced the positive pole. The transfer cassette was placed
in chamber and remaining 20 % MeOH/TG buﬀer was poured onto cassette. The transfer
was run for 1.5 h at 30 V.
Ab staining: Following transfer, the membrane was removed from cassette and washed
with 20 ml ﬁltered Tris Buﬀered Saline-0.1% Tween20 (TBST) buﬀer in a plastic con-
tainer. TBST was removed and membrane was blocked 20 ml with ﬁltered TBST 1% BSA
buﬀer for 2 h at 4  on a shaker. Solution was poured oﬀand membrane was incubated
with 20 ml 1:1000 dilution of primary mAb, either anti-mouse STAT3 or anti-mouse β-
Actin, in TBST 1 % BSA buﬀer O/N at 4  on a shaker.
Membrane development: Primary mAb solution was poured oﬀmembrane, which was sub-
sequently washed with 20 ml ﬁltered TBST for 10 min. Membrane was then incubated
with 20 ml 1:2000 secondary Ab in ﬁltered TBST 1 % BSA buﬀer for 1 h at RT. Solution
was poured oﬀand membrane washed with 20 ml ﬁltered TBST for 5 min three times. To
the membrane, a 2 ml 1:1 detection reagent mix of western blotting substrate was added
and left to react for two minutes. The membrane was then transferred to the LI-COR
Odyssey® FC gel imager and imaged using the 600 and 700 nm and chemiluminescence
channels.

==PAGE:157==
Appendix C
High concentration ELISA
Standard IL-6 samples are included in ELISA kits, however all incubations and exper-
iments involving IL-6 have been conducted using rh IL-6/CF, see Section 8.1. It was
therefore of interest to determine the applicability of rh IL-6 as standard samples with
known concentrations in ELISA versus the provided standard IL-6 from the kits as well
as determining the maximum [IL-6] applicable for ELISA.
In this high concentration ELISA, standard 2-fold dilution series samples were prepared
using provided Standard IL-6 (starting at 2000 pg/ml) and rh IL-6 (starting at 2000 pg/ml
and at 140,000 pg/ml). 140,000 pg/ml were chosen as the high concentration ELISA sam-
ple as per literature [79] and to cover entire [IL-6] range down to ∼2000 pg/ml IL-6.
ELISA was performed as per protocol, see Section 8.1.2. A schematic setup of the 96-well
plate is overviewed in Table C.1 with the concentrations used for each triple-determined
standard curve shown. During the experiment, rapid colour development upon addition
of substrate solution was observed, in particular for samples with [IL-6] = 140,000 pg/ml.
Colour development was stopped almost immediately after substrate addition. Some-
what slower development was seen in wells with [IL-6] = 2000 pg/ml and development
was stopped after approximately 10-12 min. The rapid development is undoubtedly due
to the higher [IL-6] and thus higher concentration of conjugated HRP enzymes, converting
TMB to the turquoise oxTMB. The standard curves generated are visualised in Figure C.1.
Table C.1: Schematic 96-well plate setup of high concentration ELISA.

==PAGE:158==
APPENDIX C. HIGH CONCENTRATION ELISA
Jeppe Sejerø Holm
Figure C.1:
Standard curves generated from high concentration ELISA
study.
From Figure C.1 it is evident that [IL-6] of <2000 pg/ml provide basis for linear standard
curves, whereas for concentration above this threshold no increasing absorbance with
increasing concentration is observed.
The trend may be due to oversaturation of the
ELISA plate prohibiting higher [IL-6] of inducing an equally higher absorbance, indicating
the maximum sensitivity of this ELISA at ∼2000 pg/ml IL-6. Additionally, only a slightly
higher absorbance is observed when utilising rh IL-6 compared to the provided standard
IL-6 from the ELISA kit, meaning that rh IL-6 is applicable for use as reference IL-6
in future ELISAs. In summary, samples with [IL-6] <2000 pg/ml can be analysed using
ELISA.
VI
==PAGE:159==
Appendix D
Incubation ELISA
D.1
Incubation setup
A standard setup of IL-6+/Cat G+ incubations measured by ELISA is seen in Table D.1.
IL-6+/CG+ denotes incubation samples and IL-6+ and Cat G+ the respective reference
samples. The serine protease inhibitor Pefabloc® SC (Pefabloc) was used to inhibit the
activity of Cat G and thus stop the reaction after the appropriate time. The potential
eﬀect of Pefabloc on ELISA measurements was investigated by addition of Pefabloc to
half the reference samples, denoted by the subscript P in Table D.1. To the remaining
half an equal volume of reaction buﬀer was added. Additionally, one well per time point
was dedicated to sole addition of Pefabloc following incubation of reaction buﬀer, wells
H3, H6 and H9 in Table D.1.
Pefabloc contains the active compound being the serine protease inhibitor AEBSF. Ac-
cording to vendor speciﬁcations, Pefabloc is useful in 0.1-1 mM range [78].
Previous
literature have suggested usefulness of [Pefabloc] of 1-8 mM for [Cat G] of ∼33 µg/ml
[82], 10 mM Pefabloc for 20 µl highly Cathepsin G rich bronchoalveolar lavage ﬂuid sam-
ples from chronic obstructive pulmonary disease patients [139] as well as use of 100 mM
DFP for [Cat G] of 50 µg/ml [140]. As Cat G concentration were in the range of 2.8-15
ng/ml and thus signiﬁcantly lower than used in the above literature, addition of 0.1 mM
Pefabloc solution was deemed as suﬃcient excess to ensure complete inhibition of Cat G
enzymes.
D.2
Incubation ELISA data
Data from incubation ELISA study 2, reported in Figure 3.2.
